    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2142675609" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2142675609" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2142675609?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction">women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2142675609&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142675609" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3286417794241256976"><i>"To Fitz and the Fool, my best friends for 20 years."</i><br/><br/>Hoo boy, you know it's gonna be a rough one when the dedication makes you want to curl up in a little ball and weep for a bit, huh? Spoilers and overwraught feelings follow.<br/><br/><b>So What's It About?</b><br/><br/>Fitz, the Fool and their rag-tag group of companions forge onwards on their desperate quest of vengeance for his daughter's murder, encountering old and new allies and fresh dangers. Unbeknownst to Fitz, Bee still lives and fights against her captors with</span>
  <span id="freeText3286417794241256976" style="display:none"><i>"To Fitz and the Fool, my best friends for 20 years."</i><br /><br />Hoo boy, you know it's gonna be a rough one when the dedication makes you want to curl up in a little ball and weep for a bit, huh? Spoilers and overwraught feelings follow.<br /><br /><b>So What's It About?</b><br /><br />Fitz, the Fool and their rag-tag group of companions forge onwards on their desperate quest of vengeance for his daughter's murder, encountering old and new allies and fresh dangers. Unbeknownst to Fitz, Bee still lives and fights against her captors with a fierce determination all her own. They share a terrible destination, and this final quest will demand more from Fitz than any that has come before.<br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />I've followed FitzChivalry Farseer's story through three trilogies. He has grown from a tiny boy sleeping with the puppies to a man reeling with the loss of his beloved wolf, from a lovestruck youngster to a father and grandfather, from an assassin's apprentice to a man who can kill without a second thought. It all comes to a head in Assassin's Fate, and this review is a greater struggle for me than any that I've written so far. I know that I won't be able to sufficiently express what Fitz and his companions have come to mean to me over the thousands of pages I've spent with them, but I still owe it to them and to Robin Hobb to try my best.<br /><br />As we begin I want to take a second to think about how much has changed for Fitz and the Fool throughout their stories. They have shaken the world several times over as Prophet and Catalyst, and the process of doing so has changed them both irrevocably. The Fool is no longer the acerbic enigma cartwheeling around the room with Ratsy, and Fitz is no longer the stubborn, reckless boy dreaming of Molly in her red skirts. At this point, they have both died and returned, suffered loss and torture and pain of the worst kind, and their suffering has marked them both. As Fitz puts it, they are broken:<br /><br /><i>"She would be as broken as the Fool and I were. Something inside my chest hurt at the thought. My voice creaked. “Well. Who wouldn’t break? I broke. You broke.”<br /><br />“And we both emerged stronger.”<br /><br />“We both emerged,” I said, modifying his words."</i><br /><br />Fitz's characterization is, in my opinion, a masterclass in how to write a man who has experienced trauma, loss, ostracization and insecure attachments from a young age. We all know that he can be an infuriating protagonist, but I think that many of the things that make him infuriating also make him a psychologically accurate portrait of a man stuck in deep patterns of self-loathing, self-sabotage and cognitive distortions.<br /><br /><i>"I was never sure I understood what Regal’s torture had done to me. Part of me had died in that cell, both literally and figuratively. I was alive today. I’d never know if I’d lost more than what I had found. Useless to wonder."</i><br /><br />It's there in his reckless fight-or-flight responses and his obsessive chronicling of his past, repeating the stories of what has happened to him as if he can force it to make sense. It's there in his inability to confront information that threatens the security of his worldview - people often say that this makes him stupid, but he's only stupid to the extent that struggling with deep cognitive distortions makes someone stupid. (In my opinion, it doesn't.) It's there in his own sense of worthlessness and incompetence:<br /><br /><i>“I was dying. And I had never been enough for anything.”</i><br /><br />And, perhaps the most heartbreakingly, it's there in the way that he sabotages relationships and holds himself apart from the people that he loves and is loved by in return. As Bee reflects:<br /><br /><i>"He did not feel he deserved anything from me. Not to touch me or even to say that he loved me, for he had failed so badly at being my father. It stunned me. It was like a second wall beyond his Skill-walls, something that prevented him from believing that anyone could love him."</i><br /><br />But the Fitz books are essentially the story of how he tries to shape the lives of those around him for the better in little ways and big ways despite his own deep flaws and damage. He gets back up, and he does good, and he continues to love and fight and fix his mistakes to the extent that he is capable. A commenter in r/Fantasy (who I would mention by name if I could remember it) said something along the lines of this: "Fitz deserved better for every line of every book." He did.<br /><br />Bee is such a ferocious, peculiar, tenacious little soul. I never would have thought that anyone else's voice would be welcome to me in a Fitz book, but she stands as proof that I was incorrect. I clutched every one of her little victories close and savored her growing resourcefullness and realization of her power as a White Prophet:<br /><br /><i>"Bee. Nothing happens to you. You happen to everything."</i><br /><br />I especially loved her friendship with Thick. I think a lesser author would have created a more positive relationship between her and the Fool and I must admit that I wanted it to happen for both their sakes, but it's a testament to how well-drawn the characters and their relationships are that they clashed the way they did due to Bee's resentment of him.<br /><br />Ultimately, Assassin's Fate made me realize just how much I have come to care for nearly every character that has been written into the Realm of the Elderlings, because the book touches upon each of their lives for at least a moment or two. Alise and Leftrin are still happy and aboard the Tarman while Althea and Brashen are still happy and aboard Paragon, Carson and Sedric are PARENTS, as are Thymara and Tats, Malta and Reyn, Nettle and Riddle and Dutiful and Elliania. Rapskal is just as annoying as ever! Wintrow finally realizes that it isn't going to happen with Etta! We say goodbye to Kettricken, Chade, and even Verity, and I'd be lying if I said I didn't cry my eyes out at the return of Nighteyes:<br /><br /><i>"How is the hunting where you are?<br /><br />It will be better with you."</i><br /><br />The book manages to visit these characters from the past without detracting from the story in the present, and the story in the present would mean very little without everything and everyone that has built up to it. The stories of the dragons and the liveships are beautifully resolved, but we are left to wonder about the cycles of violence that we have seen over the course of these stories and whether another cycle of violence has been set in motion with the dragon's and Bee's merciless destruction of the Whites and their servants.<br /><br />As much as it is a goodbye to the entire world of the Realm of the Elderlings, it is more than anything a goodbye to Fitz and the Fool, beloved friends together in adventure after adventure for decades, and now facing what lies beyond life within the Skill together in an ending that is as bittersweet as it is perfect. Listen, I'm not going to sit here in this shitty hostel kitchen in Stockholm and lie to you now, after everything we've been through together: I cried harder about this book than I've ever cried about anything fictional before. I cried when Chade died and resurfaced in the Skill stream with a resounding "MY BOY!" When Fitz started to tell Bee his story in words that echoed the beginning of Assassin's Apprentice and we finally came full circle, I cried. I cried when Kettricken said goodbye to Nighteyes. I cried as Fitz poured more and more of himself into the stone and became more and more distant to his loved ones. I cried when all that was left was his knowledge that he belonged with the Fool, and you KNOW I sobbed my heart out at those last lines:<br /><br /><i>'“There’s something stalking us. Off to the side of the road, moving through the forest.” Kettricken smiled.'</i><br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />There have been so many incredible female characters throughout these books, and what I realized with this final book is how they are all "powerful female characters" in their own ways, but none of those ways of being female characters are exactly the same. Malta, Etta, Althea, Kettricken, Alise, Thymara, Molly, Nettle, Amber, Starling, Spark, and Bee are all incredibly interesting, dynamic and different female characters, and the fact that this diversity manages to exist in a series of books where 9/17 books have had a male protagonist really says something to me about Hobb's abilities as a writer.<br /><br />The main thing that I want to underscore in this section, though, is that I think the Fool is a great representation of a gay and genderfluid character. He has always been upfront about his love for Fitz being all-encompassing and including romantic love. In Assassin's Fate, the genderfluidity becomes the most apparent it's been: he repeatedly switches genders and pronouns throughout the book and is equally comfortable whatever gender he presents as. Fitz wonders repeatedly throughout the books if the Fool is just another false guise, and to this the Fool responds that he has allowed Fitz to see as much of himself as anyone alive. Neither is a guise; Amber and the Fool are two equally real parts of the sum of the person that he is. What's more is that Fitz has come a really, really long way in overcoming his internalized issues with the Fool being queer. When someone asks him about it, this is what he says:<br /><br /><i>“He was King Shrewd’s jester when I was a boy. The Fool. Then Lord Golden. Mage Gray. And now Lady Amber. All different. Yet always my friend.” I reached for honesty. “But when I was your age, it would have bothered me a great deal. It doesn’t now because I know who he is. And who I am, and who we are to each other. That doesn’t change, no matter what name he wears or what garb he dons... I know he’s my friend.”</i><br /><br />As for his love for Fitz and Fitz's love for him, I'd argue that theirs is one of the most meaningful, complex and beautiful relationships in all of fantasy:<br /><br /><i>“We were one thing. A whole thing. You and I and Nighteyes. I felt a strange sort of peace. As if all the parts of me were finally in one place. All the missing bits that would make me a complete…thing.”</i><br /><br />The bonds between Fitz, the Fool and Nighteyes and their incredible characterization have always been at the heart of these books and what makes them so wonderful. Wherever they are now, the three of them are together and as long as that is the case, it accounts for most of the "sweet" in the "bittersweet" of this ending.<br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br /><br />Robin Hobb is a pseudonym for Margaret Astrid Lindholm Ogden. She grew up in California and Alaska, and studied at the University of Denver before returning to Alaska. Her early career as a writer focused on books for young readers, and she began to write speculative fiction in the 1970s and 80s. Her first book, Harpy's Flight, was published in 1983, but her first book as Robin Hobb was Assassin's Apprentice, published in 1995. It is under this name that she has gained acclaim as one of the world's most popular and critically acclaimed epic fantasy writers. She currently lives in Tacoma, Washington.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3286417794241256976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922690399" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2537642648765079039"><i>
  <b>“Don’t do what you can’t undo, until you’ve considered what you can’t do once you’ve done it.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Five sub-series, sixteen main volumes, THE BEST fantasy series ever written and now it’s done.<br/><br/>No story read so far affected me as much as this one did. I loved every word of it. I loved how this last volume connects all the loose ends from all fifteen which precede it. If you only read Fitz' story from <i>Farseer</i>, <i>Tawny Man</i> and <i>The Fitz and the Fool</i> and skipped <i>Liveship Traders</i> and <i>Rain Wild Chronicles</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2537642648765079039" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Don’t do what you can’t undo, until you’ve considered what you can’t do once you’ve done it.”</b>
</i><br><br>Five sub-series, sixteen main volumes, THE BEST fantasy series ever written and now it’s done.<br><br>No story read so far affected me as much as this one did. I loved every word of it. I loved how this last volume connects all the loose ends from all fifteen which precede it. If you only read Fitz' story from <i>Farseer</i>, <i>Tawny Man</i> and <i>The Fitz and the Fool</i> and skipped <i>Liveship Traders</i> and <i>Rain Wild Chronicles</i>, you will not get the full picture of the events in this one. It intertwines both narratives in an epic ending so majestically weaved that I’m in awe. Should I say how much I cried over it? A lot. No book ever made me cry this much. Ever. But I so rejoiced in it that it was all worth it. And I can’t say anything else about it; I’m at a loss for words.<br><br>Mrs. Robin Hobb, Chapeau! You are The Queen of words.<br><br><br>LE: Robin Hobb on saying goodbye (or not) to Fitz &amp; Co: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cosmopolitan.com/entertainment/books/a9655606/robin-hobb-interview/">http://www.cosmopolitan.com/entertain...</a><br><br>----------<br>Finally here !!! I barely started it but I'm loving it already :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493915987i/22666654.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1991806201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991806201" />
    <a title="Shelly K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53635269-shelly-k"><img alt="Shelly K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460719433p2/53635269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991806201?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly K" href="/user/show/53635269-shelly-k">Shelly K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53635269-shelly-k?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53635269-shelly-k?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53635269-shelly-k?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53635269-shelly-k?shelf=i-need">i-need</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991806201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12512870723094243186">In my first year of university a professor told me that fantasy writing is like imaginative masterbation. (What a jackass.) I took that to mean he believed fantasy to lack substance and was therefore unsatisfying.<br/><br/>I get that there is little love for fantasy in literary circles but THIS. This series has been one of the most satisfying reading experiences I have ever had, of anything I've ever read, be it literary or genre fiction. <br/><br/>Five trilogies, sixteen main volumes, and each book was a joy to re</span>
  <span id="freeText12512870723094243186" style="display:none">In my first year of university a professor told me that fantasy writing is like imaginative masterbation. (What a jackass.) I took that to mean he believed fantasy to lack substance and was therefore unsatisfying.<br /><br />I get that there is little love for fantasy in literary circles but THIS. This series has been one of the most satisfying reading experiences I have ever had, of anything I've ever read, be it literary or genre fiction. <br /><br />Five trilogies, sixteen main volumes, and each book was a joy to read. All of them together was a fine art. <br /><br />What a journey this has been with so many highs and lows. And what an ending this book was. I never anticipated this ending, but thinking back, it couldn't have ended any other way. Every important character, every bit of history and lore and individual adventure came together in this final instalment. <br /><br />It is not only the journey that made this reading experience so amazing but the hypnotic writing, the maddening real characters, the complex relationships and the commentaries on sex and gender. I still don't know if the Fool was a man or a woman but after wondering about it for sixteen books have been led to accept the Fool as just being. <br /><br />Hobb could have written anything but she chose to write fantasy and I am grateful for it.<br /><br />If you have any love for fantasy I highly recommend the full experience and read these in proper order:<br /><br />Farseer Trilogy<br />Liveship Trilogy<br />Tawny Man Trilogy<br />Rain Wilds Chronicles<br />Fitz and the Fool<br /><br />It's pure art.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12512870723094243186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1558178287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1558178287" />
    <a title="Emily " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2377230-emily"><img alt="Emily " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486778976p2/2377230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1558178287?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily " href="/user/show/2377230-emily">Emily </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30698254-assassin-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2377230-emily?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1558178287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15755868101344242023">I'm tempted to give this 5stars because FitzChivalry is my probably my very favorite book character of all time, and the ending did not disappoint (I've spent the last two hours crying my eyes out) - BUT, in true Robin Hobb style the first 60% of the book was a drag. In fact, my sisters are reading this book and warned me not to spoil it, and I told them that up to that point, I couldn't spoil anything even if I tried - NOTHING had happened. It was reminiscent of the last book of the 1st trilogy</span>
  <span id="freeText15755868101344242023" style="display:none">I'm tempted to give this 5stars because FitzChivalry is my probably my very favorite book character of all time, and the ending did not disappoint (I've spent the last two hours crying my eyes out) - BUT, in true Robin Hobb style the first 60% of the book was a drag. In fact, my sisters are reading this book and warned me not to spoil it, and I told them that up to that point, I couldn't spoil anything even if I tried - NOTHING had happened. It was reminiscent of the last book of the 1st trilogy where it was just tons of travel time and introspection until the last 25% of the book and then BAM, non stop action and emotion.<br /><br />I will say that Bee really grew on me in this last book. I really disliked her in books one and two, but she was great in this book. And little Perseverance - he was so adorable. One of my new favorites. So many people in this series overall that I just loved and were so memorable - Verity, Kettricken, Nighteyes, Chade, Burrich - even Motley! Oddly there were others that I feel I should have liked, but just never really did. Dutiful's wife, Nettle, Fool as Amber, Bee when she was young. Molly most of all - I never liked her. Am I the only one that never really "felt" the relationship with her and Fitz?<br /><br />One of the things I didn't like is I felt like the book took too much time with Rainwild and Liveship stuff. I liked those characters, but those sections went on forever and were totally irrelevant to anyone that didn't read the Liveship or Rainwild books. It felt a little indulgent to me that Hobb seemed to want to write a sequel to their story too, but was foisting it on me in a place I didn't want it (in a Fitz book). <br /><br />If I could rate the last 35% of the book - this would be 5 stars. The ending was everything you would want, everything is wrapped up nicely. You'll probably feel like me, absolutely wrung out emotionally, sad to say goodbye to old friends (and let's be honest - their story is done - time to let them go), but satisfied with how things turn out. <br /><br />Despite my nitpicks, this series will always be one of my absolute favorites of all time. The characters are fantastic, Hobb can write so beautifully and emotionally. The magic system is great (skilling, wit, dragons, elderlings), the world is so complete and complex. I feel as I do every time I end a beloved series - bittersweet that it ended, and wondering if I'll ever find another series that will ever be so dear to me!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15755868101344242023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12074783745923006909">For info, I'm usually a very mild mannered person who wouldn't dream of writing a negative review but after more than a year since reading the final Fitz and the Fool book I'm still hurt, angry and upset at the harsh and ham fisted way the final book was written. One would almost think Hobb had no love at all for Fitz and the Fool and their ending, it was almost like somebody else had written the final books, someone with little knowledge of the previous books, the characters and their struggles</span>
  <span id="freeText12074783745923006909" style="display:none">For info, I'm usually a very mild mannered person who wouldn't dream of writing a negative review but after more than a year since reading the final Fitz and the Fool book I'm still hurt, angry and upset at the harsh and ham fisted way the final book was written. One would almost think Hobb had no love at all for Fitz and the Fool and their ending, it was almost like somebody else had written the final books, someone with little knowledge of the previous books, the characters and their struggles. But hey, that's just my opinion and after looking at the reviews I'm in the minority. All I can say is that I still feel deeply hurt at the way the final book dealt with our beloved characters and I've spent years of my life reading about them. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467822720i/19635011.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403718403" />
    <a title="Marielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45124366-marielle"><img alt="Marielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572516394p2/45124366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403718403?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marielle" href="/user/show/45124366-marielle">Marielle</a>

<div id="review_1984011670" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984011670" />
    <a title="Phee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26480778-phee"><img alt="Phee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580467651p2/26480778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984011670?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phee" href="/user/show/26480778-phee">Phee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007444274" href="/book/show/29356969-assassin-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984011670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3553882369686639470">** Spoiler Free **<br/><br/>I can't even begin to describe what this series means to me. <br/>I started it over two years ago. I DNF'd Assassins Apprentice twice before trying it one last time. Fate decided I needed to find Fitz and the Fool then. I read the Farseer trilogy over several months. Then I fell into a deep depression. I didn't read for almost a year, not one page. <br/>After I healed, this series was waiting for me. I put myself back together, like Fitz had to put himself back together so many times. It</span>
  <span id="freeText3553882369686639470" style="display:none">** Spoiler Free **<br /><br />I can't even begin to describe what this series means to me. <br />I started it over two years ago. I DNF'd Assassins Apprentice twice before trying it one last time. Fate decided I needed to find Fitz and the Fool then. I read the Farseer trilogy over several months. Then I fell into a deep depression. I didn't read for almost a year, not one page. <br />After I healed, this series was waiting for me. I put myself back together, like Fitz had to put himself back together so many times. It's taken me 5 months but I have finished this 16 book series in its entirety. I've never been so passionate, nor so emotional about a book or characters in my life. <br /><br />Fitz and the Fool represent so much more to me than I can put into words. They are two parts of the same being, one isn't complete without the other. The Catalyst and the White Prophet. Their relationship goes beyond explanation. Throughout the books many characters ask them what they mean to each other. They can never seem to explain it well. Boyhood friend, lover, brother. I have used the word soulmate to describe them in the past and I think that is the best word. They love each other deeply, perhaps one of them loves the other in a more romantic sense, but they both love each other. They complete each other and they live for one another. They can't bare to be parted by death, one can't die and let the remain living. It's not right. <br /><br />The ending. Well I knew it would end this way from Assassins Quest. Fitz's goal had always been the same. His road was never going to be easy. The hints are there throughout the Fitz and the Fool trilogies. There is so much foreshadowing for this story. From earlier books and in this one itself. I think it's fair to say that all of the little pieces of information that are at the beginning of each chapter are terribly important. Sometimes you don't want to read them because you want to get straight back into the action. But these little pieces tell you the fates of our heroes many times. If you know how listen. <br /><br />I can't write a review for this book. I can't even begin to make sense of what I feel. All I know is this series is a massive part of me. It will stay with me forever. A memory etched into me like carving stone. <br />This is the first book that made me cry. Normally when I get emotional whilst reading I get tears in my eyes. I have never properly cried. <br />This book made me sob, full on ugly cry. I have never been so emotional from reading a book. <br />This last book was a joy to read and it was painful. Bittersweet. But perfect. Things come full circle, and are finished at last. I'm not going to spoil it but that scene where two (or three depending on how you look at it) become one was beautiful. My heart aches every time I read it again. I'm so happy it ended this way, even if it's not necessarily a happy ending. <br /><br /><br />And for those that are curious. My top three books out of the entire 16 book series are:<br /><br />1) Fool's Quest<br />2) Assassin's Fate<br />3) Assassin's Quest <br /><br />"Then it was finished. Something finally complete, as it should have been."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3553882369686639470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1995379328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995379328" />
    <a title="Wol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol"><img alt="Wol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518815855p2/5973651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1995379328?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol">Wol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973651-wol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1995379328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16719815683653256411">Ok, so by "in a few days" I apparently meant "in over a week". <br/><br/>So now I'm finally emerging from what is probably the most debilitating book hangover I have ever experienced, I'll write an actual review. I always try to keep my reviews spoiler free, but with so much riding on the events of this entry that's much more difficult than usual. What that means here is that I have to keep it super vague. <br/><br/>Throughout my Hobb reviews, many times I have likened the Realm of the Elderlings to an intricate ta</span>
  <span id="freeText16719815683653256411" style="display:none">Ok, so by "in a few days" I apparently meant "in over a week". <br><br>So now I'm finally emerging from what is probably the most debilitating book hangover I have ever experienced, I'll write an actual review. I always try to keep my reviews spoiler free, but with so much riding on the events of this entry that's much more difficult than usual. What that means here is that I have to keep it super vague. <br><br>Throughout my Hobb reviews, many times I have likened the Realm of the Elderlings to an intricate tapestry in which Hobb slowly and methodically weaves together her ideas and events into a larger picture that isn't immediately apparent. Each part of the tapestry is beautiful in its own right, but the larger picture emerges very slowly. Until now. We learn <i>so much</i> about the world in Assassin's Fate that it's dizzying. Seeds she planted 12+ books ago come to fruition. <br><br>I feel sorry for anyone who didn't read Liveships or Rain Wilds because they are not the ones who will get the most out of Assassin's Fate. There are new faces and old friends, and things haven't necessarily developed for them in ways you might expect. They will all be hugely impacted by the events of this book. For some, their whole way of life will have to change. Worlds collide for two facets of the Fool with awkward, funny and occasionally terrifying results. It's a masterpiece.<br><br><b>About The Ending (stop here if you consider my emotions a spoiler), AKA:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495645084i/22840925.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was fitting. As soon as I realized how it would end, I knew it had been inevitable from the very beginning. That didn't prevent me from weeping my way through the last 100 pages, mind you. Granted I'm an emotional reader, but Hobb in particular sure knows how to play my heartstrings like a fiddle. Well enough that my husband took one look at me, said, "Oh no! Oh honey!" and immediately brought me both chocolate and a glass of whiskey. He's good like that. <br><br>If this is the last in the Elderlings novels (and that's a very big "if"), it was a magnificent end to a magnificent series. If it's not (and I do hope it's not), I very much look forward to seeing the consequences of the changes that were made to the world in this entry. <br><br>Either way, this was a hell of a ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16719815683653256411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1950040384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1950040384" />
    <a title="Andi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1339848-andi"><img alt="Andi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587604824p2/1339848.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1950040384?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andi" href="/user/show/1339848-andi">Andi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950040384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2028412355907579723">To prepare myself for the end of Assassins Fate, I had someone spoil me on what Fitz’ fate was.<br/><br/>It is perhaps the one time in my life that I regret knowing a spoiler. Looking back, if I didn’t know, I think I would be crying harder and in a funk for weeks. However, because I knew, and because I was prepared, I think I took it better.<br/><br/>Do not misinterpret my words! Of course, it has a happy ending – it has the ending that I wanted it to have… just, perhaps, not exactly the way I planned it. My words</span>
  <span id="freeText2028412355907579723" style="display:none">To prepare myself for the end of Assassins Fate, I had someone spoil me on what Fitz’ fate was.<br /><br />It is perhaps the one time in my life that I regret knowing a spoiler. Looking back, if I didn’t know, I think I would be crying harder and in a funk for weeks. However, because I knew, and because I was prepared, I think I took it better.<br /><br />Do not misinterpret my words! Of course, it has a happy ending – it has the ending that I wanted it to have… just, perhaps, not exactly the way I planned it. My words are vague I know. But I think you need to trust me on this. When you read all the books over, you can easily see this was the path it was going to take and you accept it because it’s the fitting path and the path that needed to happen. But did it need to happen now? Hrm.<br /><br />It is a depressing book, for sure. The tone and the fact that it’s ‘the end’ is enough to depress someone. Originally in my review I was going to give this a five star read, but I’m settling on a 3.5 (between three and four stars) because this book was a mess.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />For the first time, I felt how some readers felt when it came to Fitz. All he did was whine and cry. I mean, sure he lost his daughter and at one point in the book he thinks his daughter is dead, but I couldn’t believe how many times he was telling everyone he wanted to die and or wanted to end it in a blaze of glory. For someone who has friends and a family that still exists, you sure have a funny way of forgetting that they exist.<br /><br />Bee is an irksome little girl. I know she felt as though she thought her father never loved her and loved The Fool more. That may be true, but I’m sure he most certainly loves her if he’s on his way to Clerres for her. At one point she says something truly hurtful to The Fool … and after all her chapters of accepting her fate as the “Destroyer”, that ruined her character development for me. <br /><br />I really loved Amber during Liveship, so seeing me take Fitz side regarding her was a bit of a shocker. Then again, The Fool was all over the place like Fitz. He was so dead set on revenge that he just abandoned ship on their way of trying to get into the castle/fortress where the Whites are. What was the point of bringing Fitz with you, Fool? Seems you had everything planned.<br /><br />There are some unanswered questions. The fact that Pillkrop lives and broke off from the destruction of Clerres with a few whites is a bit of puzzlement for the future. He told Fitz and the Fool that the Whites should continue to exist and return to how things were before the Four fucked it all over. However, with the way the world is now…. should they?<br /><br />Where does the Skill River come from? Or, where does the silver come from? And to partner even further off that: where on earth does the Wit come from? These all never got answered and all I found out was that Clerres were stealing unhatched serpents and drawing out their ‘venom’ to make their magical drug. At least I found out what the Others beach was. Though that beach is still creepy.<br /><br />The Fool said that Dwalia was not Bee’s Catalyst. Who is? Can a white be another white’s Catalyst? Has that ever happened before? It was never really answered. So, the question remains: who is Bee’s Catalyst? Obviously her skin was shedding so it was someone in the story … I guess, again, if Robin writes a sequel series we will find out. (Edit: This was addressed in one of the comments - I like the fact that she may be her own Catalyst, did not think of that. But I'm waiting for Robin's official word on it.)<br /><br />The Skill Stone is still a mystery to me. How is it that if it was a way of travel from one place to another that people still got lost inside it? Why did they continue to use it if it was unsafe? Hopefully that will be something to dwell upon in another series.<br /><br />When Chade kicked the bucket after diving headfirst into the Skill I said ‘WELL, THAT HAPPENED’ and then ‘THANK GOD’. He was so annoying, but in retrospect, he was a very tragic figure. The private letters that Robin included that were sent to Fitz and or what Fitz wrote about in regards to him were enough to understand that he should be pitied. However, the end product was that he was so fucking annoying and he deserved losing his mind.<br /><br />So, to the basics: The reason I give the book three stars is that I believe after getting to Clerres, the story got sped up and very mismatched. Things weren’t answered or explained. As I mentioned before: Skill Stone, where the Wit comes from, motivations of some of the characters, the lack of including some of the characters from other books, and the ending that should have happened but seemed to happen too soon…<br /><br />If there ends up being a sneaky book four out of this, I’ll give it a four-star rating. Again, it was the ending that it was meant to be, but probably not at this moment. <br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2028412355907579723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1358117287" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1358117287" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1358117287?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101912812" href="/book/show/34942226-assassin-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sff-audio">sff-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=elderlings">elderlings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358117287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7409829813273283766"><b>Executive Summary:</b> There is not much I can say about this book without getting into spoilers, or making statements that may lead people to guess at their meaning. What I can say is much like Ms. Hobb's previous works, this book made me feel. A lot. <br/><br/><b>Audiobook:</b> Elliot Hill is a pretty good narrator. He can be a bit soft spoken however. And he's not great at female voices. I rather wish he didn't try. Still it's more good than bad, and I do think he adds something to the narration that makes the au</span>
  <span id="freeText7409829813273283766" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> There is not much I can say about this book without getting into spoilers, or making statements that may lead people to guess at their meaning. What I can say is much like Ms. Hobb's previous works, this book made me feel. A lot. <br /><br /><b>Audiobook:</b> Elliot Hill is a pretty good narrator. He can be a bit soft spoken however. And he's not great at female voices. I rather wish he didn't try. Still it's more good than bad, and I do think he adds something to the narration that makes the audio worthwhile. If you liked him in the previous books, you should like him here.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />This book was difficult for me to rate. I don't give out 5 stars easily, and normally when I do it's a no-brainer. This one not so much. The book has some pacing issues, especially early on. I have no idea of the final page count, but in audio it's nearly 40 hours long. Ms. Hobb's books have always been on the slower side, but there were points in this book where it was a bit too much. That's only a minor gripe though.<br /><br />FitzChivarly Farseer is one of the most real character I ever read. When this series was announced I was both excited and nervous to get to spend more time with him. What terrible things would Ms. Hobb do to him this time? She has really put him through the ringer over the years. However my desire to spend time with him again outweighed my fear.<br /><br />When the series started, I was not happy about the addition of Bee's chapters. At its conclusion, I'm still a bit torn on them, but I think the story could not have been told otherwise. I think part of me was just irritated to have to spend any time in the book away from Fitz. In addition to Fitz, it was really great to see some old friends again, some of whom I never expected to see.<br /><br />This book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23157777.Fool_s_Quest__The_Fitz_and_The_Fool___2_" title="Fool's Quest (The Fitz and The Fool, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Quest</a> before it, rewards those who have read the entire Elderlings series, not just the Fitz books. If you haven't read Liveship Traders and Rainwild Chronicles, I highly recommend you do so first. There is so much that'll you be missing if you don't.<br /><br />There isn't much else I can say without getting into spoilers beyond this: Ms. Hobb has an incredible ability to make feel strong emotions for fictional characters. Joy, anger, love, hate, cheer, sorrow. I feel so much that I'm drained. Few books do that to me, but hers seem to do it all the time, especially the Fitz books. It is for this reason I decided to give this 5 stars instead of 4.<br /><br />Prepare yourself for an emotional journey. I hope you'll find it as worth it as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7409829813273283766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6431775924481229464">This is going to be an awful review because I've been reading this series for years and 16 books later I have finished my favorite author's series. I love this series. I love these characters. I love that this book was basically a farewell tour of the world and its characters.   <span id="freeText6431775924481229464" style="display:none">This is going to be an awful review because I've been reading this series for years and 16 books later I have finished my favorite author's series. I love this series. I love these characters. I love that this book was basically a farewell tour of the world and its characters. I think that The Fitz and Fool trilogy itself might be my favorite part of The Realm of the Elderings but I love everything about it. Don't let the hype of the series deter you or make you critical of the first books, stopping you from reading the rest. It is worth it, trust me. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q+2NLxvREN8rMLjoEUkF/EZm3/LnACDRXu9/fKL6QqX1rdyozPx348pfX/pBzsG77iLhD1g1sW7o96MA2wOuUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xQQbbeXDDkUDe2R1bCP9afCopjgKsfwxlk7hQlJ2ULpzRErqMu5peeIUg2c8pDkuWOyYxbWEbY4gVj0+K4+8Tg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7394315182824978429">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText7394315182824978429" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>

</div>
